< Text>
Food was fine, of what we got. The website was updated to match the new items they were going to offer in April, but we arrived in March, which meant none of the mains we wanted we're available yet. Major disappointment, so I didn't eat. My companions found suitable substitutes, but I didn't, so I enjoyed the pretzel and that was it. We sat on their enclosed patio where they had decided to keep the heaters turned off, even though it was in the sixties. The menus were honestly filthy, I assume because they didn't want to print new ones before the menu change over, but let me tell you what isn't appetizing at all, a filthy restaurant, which is all I can extrapolate when the menus are covered in a heavy film of gross from all the hands that had fingered them before. I'll try this place again, now that the menu's changed, and hope they have five star fish and chips, which I couldn't order on this first, dissappointing trip.  It gets three stars because the waitress was nice, the food we got was fine, and I really liked the decor, and the focus on classic Los Angeles. <rating>5< /rating><review>This was my first experience with a storage company, and one that I am glad to say was positive.  From the very beginning they showed exemplary customer service - I wanted a $1 first month rent unit and unfortunately the unit I had wanted wasn't available anymore, which ended up being OK - Tammy was helpful walked me through the facility and showed me the unit I would be renting and said she would honor the $1 first months rent with that unit.  A lot of the staff who had witnessed movers treat my possessions like garbage informed of what happened and they also didn't charge me for a violation (the movers had left some items they said they would dump) and gave me time to stop by to properly dispose of the items.

Yes they may be a bit more expensive, but you really do get what you pay for in storage.  The cheaper storage places was cheap for a reason (dirty, somewhere where I didn't want to drive to, and "secure") - this facility was extremely clean (almost shockingly so) and I have no qualms with walking around barefoot.  Not a single insect or rat, it didn't smell in any way (those are some of the cleanest bathroom I've seen for this type of facility), and it was obviously secure with how you had to enter the unit.  Yes the bathroom situation does kind of suck (you can only use it during office hours), but I was told if it was left open, then the potential for homeless people waiting to be able to get into the unit and spending nights in the facility was very possible. I've never struggled with parking and I've never had to wait to use a cart.  This place also has some of the longest access hours (6am - 9pm) I've seen compared with other storage facilities whose access hours are usually the same as the office hours (or they give like an hour leeway before and after).  My friend's storage facility was only open from 7am - 5 pm and most people are getting ready for work or at work during those hours.

Simply put - incredibly clean with long hours with a great staff who actually acknowledge the fact they are providing a service to paying customers and in turn give great customer service.  I don't know who that man is who seems to have turned people off, but I've never seen him and if he is in the office then I would wait until Tammy is back (blonde).  I should also mention that although I'm not 100% sure and I've never asked, I'm almost certain that Tammy is in the office from 9am - 6pm every single day of the week. I've gone to the storage unit at all possible hours and all days throughout the week multiple times and without fail if the office was open, she was there and never once has she been grumpy or in a bad mood. I will be back for sure!<//review>< Pics>

<Rate>5<//Rate><review>I had a great experience here. I recently relocated from Old Town, San Diego to the Bay Area. I had way too much stuff and this place was just across the overpass from my former apartment. I looked up their rates and storage sizes on their website (seemed reasonable to me). I made a reservation with Tammy over email. The day of my move, I met with Rhianna who was very helpful and informative. She went over the contract, the fees, the space, and helped me pick out a lock (bring one if you don't want to buy one there).

Since then, I've been to SD a few times to unload pro audio equipment for events and also look for things I might need to bring back to the Bay. My unit was always very accessible and in a well-protected, climate controlled environment. I felt the security was top notch as well.

I moved out a couple of days ago when I realized that I had moved all my stuff out. I got rid of my shelves that day after posting them for free on craigslist. I walked into the office after my unit was emptied and asked about moving out. I think I should have given a notice, but they still accommodated me and I was out of there in less than 5 minutes.

Oh, also, make sure you read the fine print on the contracts and such. You need to get renter's insurance if you don't have it. Also, I think there's some specials advertised but that's for certain storage sizes. I took advantage of the special with a free moving truck for the day, which was helpful, but you should reserve in advance to make sure the truck is available.

Anyway, 5 stars, no doubt. The staff does a great job and the space is safe and accessible.< /review>< Pics>

<name>Paul Burgess<//name><gmap_id>0x809b3d1602d097dd:0x1ebc854d8bf8bfa6<//gmap_id>< review>
I come here once a year, but I must be insane (doing the same thing over and over again, expecting different results). Most of the people in the outer building are very nice, but the ladies inside the closed building seem to run the place and they have always been rude and their pricing is downright ridiculous! As a "thrift" store, they get their donations for free. Yet, they are higher priced on the majority of their items, than you could likely get them for retail in stores. $10-20 for run of the mill jeans, shoes anywhere from $20-150, coffee mugs $3-5, jackets will run you $20-100+. You have to be kidding me! I asked one of the ladies why they felt the prices should be so high and she straight up told me that's what they saw on eBay! Not what the items were "SOLD" for, but what people were TRYING to sell them for. I looked up a couple items and showed her what people were "actually" paying for a few items in comparison to what they had them priced for (much more) and she said she didn't care, as it was their shop and they will run it how they want. This is not eBay! You are supposed to be helping your community by offering the free donations you get, to others around your area at a fair price, when they can't afford, or don't want to pay full retail price, new.

This place is NOT a true thrift store. They are extremely greedy in their pricing and they are not here to help the community, only to take the communities donations in hopes of selling it for high profits. I always have and always will take my true business to the REAL thrift store and cat adoption shop in town, not even a mile away from this place. Please do yourself a favor and look them up instead and save the time and frustration of going through this shop. I hope this helps others and I can only hope that someday, this place will be run by someone who is fair and wants to HELP the community around them.<//review>

< review>
I've seen Wushiland Boba locations pop up in different places in the SGV. I know they have another location in Focus Plaza but I've personally never been there but since I was at the mall decided to stop in and try it since they were brand new. They are located on the first floor right next to Macy's.

With social distancing guidelines, they made the queue line up outside and only one party at a time can be inside to place an order. And they tell you to wait outside until your drink is ready.  There's a good variety of different types of drinks here but I went with something basic.

Overall, the drink was pretty good I got the green milk tea with pearls. They do put more pearls in the drink compared to most places.  At least that's what it feels like.  My sister got the milk tea with ice cream and that sounded really good too.

Right now they do have a 10% off until the end of November if you comment on Google Maps or tag them on Instagram.</review>

< text>
Had been here before with no issues. Two guys cutting hair one of whom was the owner. They usually work through their clients at a reasonable pace. However, my last visit was absolutely the worst visit I've had at a barber shop. First of all I went in on a Tuesday thinking there would be less people but that was not the case. I only had about an hour or so and I had to get back to work. But to my dismay a couple of people that I could of sworn got there after me go their haircuts first, one with the owner and the other with the other barber. I stayed cool and tried to be patient as much as possible since I would be next. But then the other barber said who's next? Like he did not know it was me. An older gentleman quickly jumped up and without even giving a second thought took him over me. One could say well you should have said "Hey I'm next" but given the fact that they had taken two guys before me I was confident they knew I was next. Part of me stayed quiet just to see how much they really cared about the order. Turns out they don't. As a side note, most if not all places know who's next and let the customers be free of the guesswork. Once the owner (Eddie) was done with his client he looked at me and grinned and said "I guess you're next". I'm thinking really? Now you're keeping track. It was too late to get a haircut because by this point it was already two hours and was late for work, but I wanted to let him know how dissatisfied I was with the service. I walked out and will not be coming back ever.  If keeping track is difficult then I suggest a number system or a sign in sheet but I'm not going to be arguing with other customers on who's next when the barbers should know.</text>

<rating>5<//rating>< Text>
I was excited to try this place! The idea of combining tapas/flights seemed perfect for a happy hour with a friend. Plus during actual happy hour it's 25% off the menu!

VIBE: located in beautiful downtown Campbell! Decent sized place with a bar and good amount of tables

SERVICE: how cute that all the waiters are like "flight attendants"! They also give you a card to flip up at the table when you need service or when you're "ready for take off". Kinda cheesy but convenient!

FOOD: if you check in on Yelp you get a free glass of champagne!

Tropical cocktails- pina colada, strawberry daiquiri and mai tai. Don't let their tiny size fool you, these were STRONG.

French fries- truffle, garlic and sweet potato each with their own dipping sauces. My favorite dip was with the sweet potato!

Mac n Cheese- classic, truffle, and bacon/jalape√±o. Surprisingly I preferred the bacon over the truffle which wasn't that flavorful.

BBQ Sliders- These were difficult to share since we had to cut these tiny messy sliders in half. But I thought they paired well with the other flights

Overall our happy hour was enjoyable, and our server didn't try to rush us to finish even though the restaurant was getting pretty crowded as it got closer to peak dinner time. I think its only worth it to come here for happy hour because for a couple of flights it added to be pretty pricy (~$60 after tip) and I didn't think the food was that unique, just insta-worthy presentation.<//Text>

< review>
Flights is not what it used to be, at least not in Los Gatos. Once, they boasted a large menu of innovative dishes, each offered in a trio (a "flight") featuring variations on a theme. Each dish was well-prepared and delicious.  Unfortunately, times change.

Flights had changed hands, and the menu, and food quality, have changed with it.  The new menu still has a few flights, but the bulk of the food is offered in "bites".  This would be fine if the quality had been maintained.  Unfortunately, the new menu is loaded with food that is bland and uninspired. The "Korean" Buffalo Chicken looked fancy on the plate, but it tasted like fried chicken nuggets drizzled in Frank's Red Hot sauce. It was mostly heat and little flavor. The sliders also looked great, but tasted rather plain, even the Chipotle Beef slider, which featured avocado and corn etole. The biggest letdown was the "Reverse Cheesecake" flight that we ordered for dessert. Essentially cheesecake in three jars, each topped with different toppings. The most flavorful part of the entire flight was the Oreo crumble on the chocolate entry.  The strawberry topping was merely adequate, and the mango topping was clearly fermented. The cheesecake itself was loose and bland.

On the plus side, the wait staff was very friendly.  Still, we likely won't be back anytime soon.<//review>

<Review>After having a sub-par experience at the Flights location in Campbell, I was hopeful that the Los Gatos location may redeem this place. I went for a birthday party with a group of girls and somehow the experience was even worse. The food was not good at all (the grilled cheese was especially disappointing- how can you mess that up so bad?), but the service was possibly the worst I've ever experienced at a restaurant. The restaurant anyway expects you to press a button to receive service which is strange to me, but we had to press the buttons over and over to get someone to come wait on our table. We ran out of water multiple times and couldn't get anyone to bring more, we waited a very long time to have someone bring a to-go box, they didn't bus our table until we left basically so as we chatted, there was just mess everywhere, and several dishes came out cold. To top it all off, the event planner told the person who planned the night that we wouldn't need to pay a minimum when she was making the reservation, yet when the bill came, there was a minimum fee added to the bill. When we approached them, they said it's non-negotiable which was frustrating enough, but they also never pro-actively presented the opportunity to us to actually order more food/dessert to meet it so we essentially were all forced to split an extra $250 that the restaurant just pocketed since we didn't know about this minimum until we were all ready to leave. To finish out the series of unfortunate events, the waitress came up to us rudely at 9:30 to tell us we needed to leave because the restaurant had been closed for 30 minutes (again, they hadn't even bussed our table so they didn't seem to be in much of a hurry and there are much nicer ways to do this). I will never return and doubt the 13 other girls will either.

<rating>5< /rating><review>Flights in Los Gatos is far superior to the Campbell location. As I have gone to both a number of times here are my comparisions.
Both restaurants: The whole concept of Flights is very cute and a food lover's dream. The decor is air travel, the servers dress like flight attendants, and there is a call button on your table airplane style. Most of the food/drinks are served in "flights" of 3, tapas style. That isnt to say you have to share and some things, like salads and flatbreads are served in normal portions.
Campbell: Limited seating and food seems to be prepared more hastily than Los Gatos. (I'll go into more detail in my review of the campbell location).
Los Gatos: Ample indoor and outdoor seating, plus bar seating. I've only visited this location during weekday lunch hours and it is never busy, though I'm not sure why. There is also ample parking between their own small lot and the large shared lot behind the restaurant.
Food: Honestly everything I've tried has been good but I most highly recommend the ceviche, steak tacos, and Stix (way bigger than they look on the menu). I don't eat gluten or dairy and there are tons of options for me. Only thing I've tried that I would probably not order again is the sliders, they do have GF buns but they are pretty dry and the burgers aren't anything exciting.

Overall, I highly recommend Flights Los Gatos for business, groups of friends or families. It is also sure to impress out of town guests.</review><pictures>None<//pictures>< response>

<userid>101839682262193572073< /userid><username>Dude</username><Time>1518457143109< /Time><Rate>3</Rate>< text>
In A Nutshell:

-Flights really took off w/ a great idea.
-They serve everything, "flight" style, think 3's.
-With that being said, I was slightly disappointed w/ the service.
-I am not sure the "team" concept works very well when if your plates stack up and each team member walks by w/ out clearing the table, possibly thinking the next team member "might do it".
-As a customer you probably shouldn't have to ask, especially at this place when you know things are going to stack up pretty fast.
-The food itself was good, but can improve.
-The waffles could be warmer and less soggy.
-The bacon and beer flight took too long to come out and the bacon soaks up the beer making it soggy.
-I really liked the eggs benedict flight and would order again.

Overall, I hate writing reviews about service, but for now this place gets 3 stars.  It can easily improve and I will give it another shot.< /text>

Flights has a fun and well executed theme and concept.  The decor is themed to the classic era of commercial aviation.  And everything on the menu comes in flights of three variations on an idea, all distinct and interesting, though you can opt to have only one or two variations if you prefer. You can probably find better single instances of anything on this menu, but if you crave diversity and variety in your dining, Flights is an excellent choice!< /text>

When I first came to Flights it was at the request of an eight year-old, so my expectations weren't very high. I'd been to the old restaurant that used to occupy the building a few times, but had never been here. It was very impressive.

The menu was wonderful, with something to fit everyone's needs. One thing to remember is that everything comes in threes (duh), so if you order some margaritas, don't be surprised when they put three in front of you!
